## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy xDS v3 Transport Protocol Implementation

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the xDS v3 transport protocol. Identify: the GrpcSubscriptionImpl adapter, the SotW (State of the World) GrpcMuxImpl, the Delta xDS NewGrpcMuxImpl, the GrpcConfigSubscriptionFactory that selects between SotW and Delta modes, and the unified XdsMux template that supports both variants.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)

- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've successfully identified all the C++ source files implementing the xDS v3 transport protocol in Envoy. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

**1. GrpcSubscriptionImpl Adapter** - The main bridge between xDS subscriptions and the underlying mux
- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_subscription_impl.h/cc`

**2. Legacy SotW Implementation** - State-of-the-World GrpcMuxImpl using DiscoveryRequest/Response
- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`

**3. Legacy Delta Implementation** - NewGrpcMuxImpl using DeltaDiscoveryRequest/Response
- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`
- Plus supporting delta subscription state files

**4. GrpcConfigSubscriptionFactory** - Selects between SotW and Delta modes
- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_subscription_factory.h/cc`

**5. Unified XdsMux Template** - Modern template-based implementation supporting both variants
- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc` (contains GrpcMuxImpl<S, F, RQ, RS>, GrpcMuxSotw, GrpcMuxDelta)
- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/subscription_state.h` (SubscriptionStateFactory template)
- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/sotw_subscription_state.h/cc` (SotwSubscriptionState)
- `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/delta_subscription_state.h/cc` (DeltaSubscriptionState)

**6. Supporting Infrastructure** - WatchMap, GrpcStream, failover handling, caching, and resource tracking

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbols, and a detailed narrative explaining the architecture of the xDS v3 transport protocol implementation in Envoy.

parallel architectures: a legacy implementation with separate SotW and Delta implementations, and a unified template-based implementation.\\n\\n## Core Components:\\n\\n### 1. GrpcSubscriptionImpl Adapter (grpc_subscription_impl.h/cc)\\nThe main adapter class that implements the `Config::Subscription` interface, serving as the bridge between xDS subscriptions (LDS, CDS, EDS, etc.) and the underlying GrpcMux implementation. This allows different resource types to multiplex onto a single gRPC stream.\\n\\n### 2. Legacy SotW Implementation (grpc_mux_impl.h/cc)\\nThe original State-of-the-World GrpcMuxImpl manages xDS v3 transport for SotW-style subscriptions using `DiscoveryRequest`/`DiscoveryResponse` protos. It handles wire-level concerns via `GrpcStream` and aggregates multiple subscriptions onto a single gRPC connection.\\n\\n### 3. Legacy Delta Implementation (new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc)\\nThe NewGrpcMuxImpl implements incremental/delta xDS using `DeltaDiscoveryRequest`/`DeltaDiscoveryResponse` protos. This is the newer implementation that sends only resource changes rather than full state, and includes WatchMap for managing per-resource-type subscriptions. Supporting files include `delta_subscription_state.h/cc` for subscription state management.\\n\\n### 4. GrpcConfigSubscriptionFactory (grpc_subscription_factory.h/cc)\\nThe factory that creates GrpcSubscriptionImpl instances. It implements `GrpcConfigSubscriptionFactory` for SotW and `DeltaGrpcConfigSubscriptionFactory` for Delta, selecting between the two based on configuration. The factory also instantiates the appropriate GrpcMux backend (legacy GrpcMuxImpl/NewGrpcMuxImpl or unified XdsMux variants).\\n\\n### 5. Unified XdsMux Template Implementation (xds_mux/)\\nA modern template-based unified implementation that supports both SotW and Delta variants through template specialization:\\n- `grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`: Contains the template `GrpcMuxImpl<S, F, RQ, RS>` parameterized by subscription state type (S), factory (F), request type (RQ), and response type (RS). Concrete specializations are `GrpcMuxSotw` and `GrpcMuxDelta`.\\n- `subscription_state.h`: Base template `SubscriptionStateFactory<T>` for creating subscription states\\n- `sotw_subscription_state.h/cc`: `SotwSubscriptionState` and `SotwSubscriptionStateFactory` for SotW subscriptions\\n- `delta_subscription_state.h/cc`: `DeltaSubscriptionState` and `DeltaSubscriptionStateFactory` for Delta subscriptions\\n\\n### 6. Supporting Infrastructure:\\n- `watch_map.h/cc`: Manages watchers (subscribers) for a single resource type, implementing SubscriptionCallbacks interface\\n- `grpc_stream.h`: Low-level gRPC streaming interface for sending/receiving xDS proto messages\\n- `grpc_stream_interface.h`: Abstract interface for gRPC streams\\n- `grpc_mux_context.h`: Context object passed to mux implementations containing dispatcher, async client, and other configuration\\n- `grpc_mux_failover.h`: Failover support for primary/secondary xDS management servers\\n- `pausable_ack_queue.h/cc`: Manages acknowledgment queuing with pause/resume support\\n- `update_ack.h`: Represents an acknowledgment to be sent back to the xDS server\\n- `xds_source_id.h/cc`: Identifies xDS resource sources for per-source tracking\\n- `eds_resources_cache_impl.h/cc`: EDS-specific resource caching implementation\\n- `grpc_collection_subscription_factory.h/cc`: Factory for xDS-TP collection-based subscriptions\\n\\n### 7. Base Interfaces:\\n- `envoy/config/grpc_mux.h`: The GrpcMux interface that both legacy and unified implementations implement, along with `GrpcStreamCallbacks<ResponseProto>` template for stream callbacks\\n- `source/common/config/null_grpc_mux_impl.h`: Null implementation of GrpcMux when no ADS is configured\\n- `envoy/config/xds_resources_delegate.h`: Extension interface for hooking into xDS resource fetch events\\n\\n## Architecture Notes:\\nEnvoy is transitioning from dual implementations (legacy `GrpcMuxImpl`/`NewGrpcMuxImpl`) toward the unified XdsMux template-based approach. The `grpc_subscription_factory.cc` selects between implementations via runtime feature flags (e.g., `envoy.reloadable_features.unified_mux`). Both approaches implement the same public `GrpcMux` interface, allowing seamless switching at runtime. The unified implementation uses template specialization to support both SotW and Delta without code duplication, with `GrpcMuxSotw` and `GrpcMuxDelta` as concrete subclasses.\"\n}\n",

Unified XdsMux Template Implementation (xds_mux/)\\nA modern template-based unified implementation that supports both SotW and Delta variants through template specialization:\\n- `grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`: Contains the template `GrpcMuxImpl<S, F, RQ, RS>` parameterized by subscription state type (S), factory (F), request type (RQ), and response type (RS). Concrete specializations are `GrpcMuxSotw` and `GrpcMuxDelta`.\\n- `subscription_state.h`: Base template `SubscriptionStateFactory<T>` for creating subscription states\\n- `sotw_subscription_state.h/cc`: `SotwSubscriptionState` and `SotwSubscriptionStateFactory` for SotW subscriptions\\n- `delta_subscription_state.h/cc`: `DeltaSubscriptionState` and `DeltaSubscriptionStateFactory` for Delta subscriptions\\n\\n### 6. Supporting Infrastructure:\\n- `watch_map.h/cc`: Manages watchers (subscribers) for a single resource type, implementing SubscriptionCallbacks interface\\n- `grpc_stream.h`: Low-level gRPC streaming interface for sending/receiving xDS proto messages\\n- `grpc_stream_interface.h`: Abstract interface for gRPC streams\\n- `grpc_mux_context.h`: Context object passed to mux implementations containing dispatcher, async client, and other configuration\\n- `grpc_mux_failover.h`: Failover support for primary/secondary xDS management servers\\n- `pausable_ack_queue.h/cc`: Manages acknowledgment queuing with pause/resume support\\n- `update_ack.h`: Represents an acknowledgment to be sent back to the xDS server\\n- `xds_source_id.h/cc`: Identifies xDS resource sources for per-source tracking\\n- `eds_resources_cache_impl.h/cc`: EDS-specific resource caching implementation\\n- `grpc_collection_subscription_factory.h/cc`: Factory for xDS-TP collection-based subscriptions\\n\\n### 7. Base Interfaces:\\n- `envoy/config/grpc_mux.h`: The GrpcMux interface that both legacy and unified implementations implement, along with `GrpcStreamCallbacks<ResponseProto>` template for stream callbacks\\n- `source/common/config/null_grpc_mux_impl.h`: Null implementation of GrpcMux when no ADS is configured\\n- `envoy/config/xds_resources_delegate.h`: Extension interface for hooking into xDS resource fetch events\\n\\n## Architecture Notes:\\nEnvoy is transitioning from dual implementations (legacy `GrpcMuxImpl`/`NewGrpcMuxImpl`) toward the unified XdsMux template-based approach. The `grpc_subscription_factory.cc` selects between implementations via runtime feature flags (e.g., `envoy.reloadable_features.unified_mux`). Both approaches implement the same public `GrpcMux` interface, allowing seamless switching at runtime. The unified implementation uses template specialization to support both SotW and Delta without code duplication, with `GrpcMuxSotw` and `GrpcMuxDelta` as concrete subclasses.\"\n}\n",
